In the event that any person commences business or initially engages in a regulated activity in the city after January 1 in any year, the tax and/or fee shall be due and payable 30 days following the commencement of the business. 
(b)  Any individual, business or practitioner subject to any occupation tax or regulatory fee imposed by this article, which is unpaid for 90 days after the date on which the payment was due, shall be subject to a penalty of ten percent of the tax or fee due. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(2), § 1(18-12)) 
State Law reference— Occupational license due day, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-16. 
Sec. 22-29. - Enforcement; violations. 
(a)  It is the duty of the clerk of the city and the police department to administer and enforce the provisions of this article, to perform all functions necessary to administer and enforce this article and to summon violators of this article to appear before the municipal court. The clerk of the city may issue executions against individuals, businesses and practitioners for taxes and fees which are due and owing. 
(b)  The clerk of the city shall issue executions against individuals, businesses and practitioners for taxes and fees which are due and owing. Such executions shall bear interest at the rate authorized by O.C.G.A. § 48-2-40 or, if such statute should be repealed, one percent per month. The lien shall cover the property of the individual, business or practitioner liable for payment of the delinquent occupation tax or regulatory fee and become fixed as of the date and time the occupation tax or regulatory fee became delinquent. The execution shall be levied by the clerk of the city upon property of the delinquent tax or fee payer located in the city and sufficient property shall be advertised and sold to pay the amount of the execution, including penalty, interest and costs. All other proceedings in relation thereto shall be as provided by this Code, the Charter of the city and the laws of the state. The defendants at execution shall have the rights of defense, by affidavit of illegality of the tax or otherwise as provided by the Charter of the city and the laws of the state in regard to tax executions. 
(c)  When a nulla bona entry has been entered upon an execution, the person against whom the entry is made shall not be allowed or entitled to have or collect any fees or charged whatever for services rendered after the entry of the nulla bona. If, at any time after the nulla bona entry has been made, the person against whom the execution issues pays the tax in full, together with all interest and costs accrued on the tax, the person may collect any fees and charges due to such person as if such person had never defaulted in the payment of the tax. 
(d)  Individuals, businesses and practitioners who fail or refuse to pay any occupation tax or regulatory fee charged pursuant to this article shall be subject to an additional fine of $100.00. 
(e)  Individuals, businesses and practitioners who fail or refuse to make a timely or truthful tax return or make available truthful and accurate information the city requests or requires for determining applicability or amount of occupation tax or regulatory fee, or for levying or collecting such occupation tax or regulatory fee shall be subject to a fine in the amount of $10.00 per 30-day period, or part thereof, during which the business or practitioner failed to file a return or during which the business or practitioner permitted an untruthful return to be on file with the city. 
(f)  All persons subject to the occupation tax or regulatory fee imposed by this article shall be required to file for and pay such tax or fee. For failure to do so, any officers or agents soliciting for or obtaining such person, the business shall be subject to the same penalty as other persons, businesses or practitioners who fail to obtain, make a return for or pay the applicable occupation tax or regulatory fee. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(2), § 1(18-13)) 
Secs. 22-30—22-46. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - INSURANCE LICENSE TAX[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Insurance license taxes, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-1 et seq. 

Sec. 22-47. - Insurers license fees. 
There is hereby levied for the year 1995 and for each year thereafter an annual license fee upon each insurer doing business within the city in the amount of $15.00. For each separate business location in excess of one not covered by section 22-48, which is operating on behalf of such insurers within the city, there is hereby levied a license fee in the amount of $15.00. For the purposes of this article, the term "insurer" means a company that is authorized to transact business in any of the classes of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 1) 
Sec. 22-48. - Insurers insuring certain risks at additional business locations. 
For each separate business location, not otherwise subject to a license fee hereunder, operated and maintained by a business organization which is engaged in the business of lending money or transacting sales involving term financing and in connection with such loans or sales offers, solicits or takes applications for insurance through a licensed agent of an insurer for insurance, said insurer shall pay an additional license fee of $10.00 per location for the year 1995 and for each year thereafter. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 2) 
Sec. 22-49. - Independent insurance agencies, brokers, etc., not otherwise licensed. 
There is hereby levied for the year 1995 and for each year thereafter an annual license fee upon independent agencies and brokers for each separate business location from which an insurance business is conducted, and which is not subject to the company license fee imposed by section 22-47, in the amount of $15.00 for each such location within the city. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 3) 
Sec. 22-50. - Gross premiums tax imposed on life insurers. 
There is hereby levied for the year 1995 and for each year thereafter an annual tax based solely upon gross direct premiums upon each insurer writing life, accident and sickness insurance within the state, in an amount equal to one percent of the gross direct premiums received during the preceding calendar year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1. The term "gross direct premiums," as used in this section, shall mean gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-4. The premium tax levied by this section is in addition to the license fees imposed by section 22-47. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 4) 
Sec. 22-51. - Gross premiums tax imposed on all other insurers. 
There is hereby levied for the year 1995 and for each year thereafter an annual tax based solely upon gross direct premiums upon each insurer, other than an insurer transacting business in the class of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(1), doing business within the state in an amount equal to 2.5 percent of the gross direct premiums received during the preceding calendar year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2. The term "gross direct premiums," as used in this section, shall mean gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-4. The premium tax levied by this section is in addition to the license fees imposed by section 22-47. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 5) 
Sec. 22-52. - Due date for license fees. 
License fees imposed in sections 22-47 and 22-48 shall be due and payable on the first day of 1995 and on the first day of each subsequent year. 
(Ord. of 12-20-1994(1), § 6) 
Secs. 22-53—22-69. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE SALES LICENSES 

Sec. 22-70. - Definitions. 
The following terms and words are hereby defined and shall be interpreted as follows: 
Beer shall mean any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other similar product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six percent alcohol by volume and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, small beer, and strong beer. The word does not include sake, known as Japanese rice wine. The term "beer" shall be synonymous with "malt beverage." 
City shall mean the City of Milner, Georgia. 
Commercial district shall mean any zoning district in the city starting with the letter "C". 
Corporation shall include both "S" corporation and "C" corporations. 
Licensee shall mean the individual to whom a license is issued or, in the case of a partnership or corporation, all partners of the partnership and all officers and directors of the corporation. 
Partnership shall include a general partnership, limited partnership, limited liability partnership, and limited liability limited partnership. 
Premises shall mean the building described in the application for a license issued hereunder to any licensee; provided, however, this definition shall not include the property or grounds upon which said building is located. 
Retail beer dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that engages in selling or handling of beer, as hereinabove defined, at retail within the city. 
Retail establishment shall mean a convenience store, grocery store, pharmacy. 
Retail wine dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that engages in selling or handling wines, as hereinabove defined, at retail within the city. 
Wholesale beer dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that sells and/or deals in beer, as hereinabove defined, to a retail beer dealer, as defined above, to or within the city. 
Wholesale wine dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that sells and/or deals in wine, as hereinabove defined, to a retail wine dealer, as defined above, to or within the city. 
Wine shall mean any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines, and like products. The term does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to the definition of wine contained in hereinabove. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-71. - Requirement of license. 
Beer and wine may be sold or distributed in the city only under a license granted by the city, upon the terms and conditions provided in this article. The city is empowered to grant the following classes of licenses: 
(1)  License for the retail sale of beer only; 
(2)  License for the retail sale of wine only; 
(3)  Combination license for the retail sale of beer and wine; 
(4)  License for the wholesale sale and distribution of beer only; 
(5)  License for the wholesale sale and distribution of wine only; and 
(6)  Combination license for the wholesale sale and distribution of beer and wine. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-72. - Application for sale or distribution. 
All persons desiring to sell or distribute beer and/or wine shall make application on the forms prescribed by the city. The content of all applications shall be sworn to by the applicant before a notary public or other officer qualified to administer oaths. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-73. - Location requirements. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person unless the premises of the proposed location is situated: 
(1)  300 feet or more from the property line of any church, synagogue, shrine, or other place used exclusively for religious services, including the chapel of a mortuary or cemetery; or 
(2)  300 feet or more from the property line of any school ground or college campus. The schools and colleges referred to herein shall include only such state, county, city, church, or other schools as teach the subjects commonly taught in the common schools and colleges of this state, and shall not include schools or colleges wherein only specialized subjects such as law, stenography, business, music, art, medicine, dentistry, vocational occupations, karate and other martial arts, performing arts, and other special subjects are taught; or 
(3)  100 feet or more from the property line of any private residence, unless such residence is itself in a commercial district; or 
(4)  300 feet or more from the property line of an alcoholic treatment center. 
(5)  100 feet or more from the property line of any branch of any public library. 
(6)  For purposes of this section, distances shall be measured by the most direct route which provides the closest and most reasonable means of travel on the ground to the front door entrance of the licensee. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008; Res. of 8-20-2008, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 22-74. - Location limited to commercial district. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person unless the premises of the proposed location is situated in a commercial zoning district. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-75. - Visibility of entrance. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to a retail beer dealer or retail wine dealer or retail beer and wine dealer unless the front entrance to the premises is clearly visible from a public street. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-76. - Off-premises consumption required. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person except for the sale or distribution of beer and/or wine in sealed containers and for consumption off the premises. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-77. - Retail sales required. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person for the retail sale of beer and/or wine unless the premises of the proposed location is a retail establishment which derives at least 50 percent of its total annual gross sales from the sale of staple foodstuffs, household supplies, meats, produce and dairy products. 
It shall be the responsibility of the licensee to ensure that this requirement is met on an annual basis and to maintain all records necessary for a validation thereof by designated city officials. A licensee's failure to maintain the required sales ratio shall constitute grounds for the revocation of such license. A licensee's failure to maintain sales and financial records sufficient to show compliance with the sales ratio required by this section shall also constitute grounds for the revocation of such license. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-78. - Age/criminal record of applicant. 
Any applicant for a license under this article shall be 25 years of age or older, an American citizen or an alien lawfully admitted for permanent residence, and have resided in the State of Georgia for a period of one year. No applicant shall have been convicted of, pled guilty to or pled nolo contendere to any felony or misdemeanor charge, other than traffic offenses, within ten years of the date of submission of the application, nor shall any such applicant have been incarcerated, on probation or on parole within five years preceding the date of submission of the application as a result of any felony conviction, plea of guilty or plea of nolo contendere. Where the applicant is a partnership or corporation, the requirements of this section shall apply to all of the applicant's partners, officers, directors, and majority shareholders. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-79. - Application contents. 
The license application shall include, but not be limited to, the name and address of the applicant; the proposed business location; the type of business to be conducted; if a partnership, the names and residence addresses of the partners; and if a corporation, the names of the directors, officers, and shareholders, the name and address of the corporation's agent for service of process, and the name and address of any other person or entity having a financial interest in the entity which is to own or operate the establishment for which a license is sought. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-80. - Surveyor certification. 
All original applications for new licenses shall include a certificate from a registered surveyor showing a scale drawing of the location of the proposed or existing premises, and stating both the straight line distance and the distance measured along the closest and most reasonable public access from the front door of the proposed or existing premises of the licensee to the building and property line of the nearest church, school, library, alcoholic treatment center, and private residence. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-81. - Compliance of new commercial structure required. 
Where a building intended for the sale of beer and/or wine is at the time of the application for such license not in existence or not yet completed, a license may be issued for such location, provided the plans for the proposed building show clear compliance with all provisions of this article and applicable provisions of the City Code. No sales shall be allowed in such establishment, however, until it has been completed in accordance with such plans. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-82. - Application fee. 
Each application for a retail beer dealer license or retail wine dealer license or combination retail beer dealer and retail wine dealer license shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable application fee in the amount of $250.00. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-83. - State license required. 
(a)  A wholesale beer dealer license or wholesale wine dealer license or combination wholesale beer dealer and wholesale wine dealer license shall be issued only to those persons who are licensed by the State of Georgia to sell and distribute beer or wine or both, as a wholesale dealer of such products. 
(b)  A retail beer dealer license or retail wine dealer license or combination retail beer dealer and retail wine dealer license shall be issued only to those persons who are licensed by the State of Georgia to sell and distribute beer or wine or both, as a retail dealer of such products. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-84. - Fingerprints. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2(c), each license application shall be accompanied by a complete set of the applicant's fingerprints. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-85. - Investigation of applicant/applicant consent thereto. 
After receipt of an application in proper form, the city shall direct an investigation to verify the contents of the application and ensure conformance with the provisions of this article. The applicant shall be given written notice of any additional data which may be required to facilitate or complete the verification process. The city manager shall prepare or direct the preparation of a report and recommendation and deliver same to the city council for its consideration. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-86. - Procedure for approval. 
After all procedures called for under this ordinance have been completed, the application shall be administratively reviewed by the city council. If it is determined that the applicant meets all standards and requirements of this article, then the license applied for shall be granted upon payment of the applicable license fee(s), unless some specific cause related to location, traffic condition, or other environmental condition shall justify refusal, and the city shall deliver by mail to the applicant a writing evidencing such approval. If it is determined that the application fails to meet all standards and requirements of this article, it shall be rejected and the applicant shall be notified by mail of the rejection stating the reasons therefore. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-87. - Issuance of license to corporation. 
Where an applicant is a corporation, the license shall be issued jointly to the corporation and to the majority shareholder, if an individual. Where the majority shareholder is not an individual, the license shall be issued jointly to the corporation and its president, as evidenced in the corporation's articles of incorporation. Where an applicant is a limited liability company, the license shall be issued to one of the company's members or managers. Where an applicant is a partnership, the license shall be issued to one of the partners, if an individual. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-88. - Corporation registered agent in city required. 
All licensees shall have and continuously maintain in the city a registered agent upon whom any required process and/or notice may be served. The licensee shall file the name of such agent along with the written consent of such agent with the city manager. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-89. - Request for hearing. 
Within 30 days of the city council's written decision to deny an application under this article, the applicant may file a request for a hearing before the city council to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-90. - Restriction on submittal of subsequent applications. 
An unsuccessful applicant for a license under this article may not submit a new application for the same location for 12 months after the date of the original application. An unsuccessful applicant may submit a new application for a different location at any time after final rejection of the prior application. No applicant shall have more than one application outstanding at the same time. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-91. - Annual license fees. 
All licenses issued shall be for the calendar year and shall be paid in accordance with the following provisions: 
(1)  The fee for a retail beer dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for a retail beer dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(2)  The fee for a wholesale beer dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for a wholesale beer dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(3)  The fee for a retail wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for a retail wine deal license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(4)  The fee for a wholesale wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for a wholesale wine dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(5)  The fee for a combination retail beer dealer and retail wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $750.00. The prorated fee for a combination retail beer dealer and retail wine dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $450.00. 
(6)  The fee for a combination wholesale beer dealer and wholesale wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $750.00. The prorated fee for a combination wholesale beer dealer and wholesale wine dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $450.00. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-92. - License expiration. 
All licenses issued hereunder shall expire on December 31 of each year unless renewed as hereinafter provided. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-93. - Renewal application. 
(a)  Licensees who desire to renew their licenses shall file an application and submit the requisite license fees to the city manager on the form prescribed by the city manager. Applications for renewal shall be filed before December 1 of each year. Renewal applications shall be reviewed by the city manager and upon investigation if there is no change in the ownership of licensee and no adverse reports from those agencies or departments required to inspect the premises of the licensee, the city manager shall issue a renewal license for the ensuing year, upon payment of the applicable license fee(s); and 
(b)  No new or renewal licenses shall be issued to any applicant who is delinquent in the payment of city taxes or fees, including, but not limited to, property taxes, alcoholic beverage excise taxes as hereinafter set forth, business license fees, or any other taxes or fees which are owned to the city by the applicant. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-94. - Excise tax. 
(a)  There is hereby imposed upon and levied against every licensed wholesale beer dealer an excise tax, in addition to the excise taxes levied by the state, as follows: 
(1)  Where malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a tax of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more than 15½ gallons, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 15½ gallons; 
(2)  Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
(b)  The excise tax levied and imposed in this section with respect to malt beverages sold or distributed by such wholesalers in the city to retailers doing business in the city shall be paid by such licensed wholesale dealers to the city on or before the tenth day of the month following the calendar month in which the beverages are sold or disposed of by such licensed wholesale dealer. Every licensee responsible for the payment of the excise tax shall file a report with the city itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of malt beverages, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. 
(c)  There is hereby imposed upon and levied against every licensed wholesale wine dealer an excise tax, in addition to the excise taxes levied by the state, a tax of $0.22 per liter, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(d)  The excise tax levied and imposed in this section with respect to wine sold or distributed by such wholesalers in the city to retailers doing business in the city shall be paid by such licensed wholesale dealers to the city on or before the tenth day of the month following the calendar month in which the wine is sold or disposed of by such licensed wholesale dealer. Every licensee responsible for the payment of the excise tax imposed by Section 23 shall file a report with the city manager itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of wine, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-95. - Hours of sale and/or delivery. 
(a)  Retail beer and/or retail wine dealers shall not engage in the sale of beer and/or wine except between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 11:45 p.m., Monday through Saturday; 
(b)  It shall be unlawful to make wholesale deliveries of beer and/or wine except between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday; and 
(c)  The retail sale of beer and/or wine is authorized on any election days. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-96. - Limitation on signage. 
No sign of any kind, painted or electronic, advertising the sale of beer or wine shall be permitted on the exterior of any licensed premises. No placard or sign of any kind which is visible from the exterior of the licensed premises shall make reference to the sale of beer or wine. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-97. - Limitation on license transfer. 
(a)  All licenses issued hereunder shall be personal to the licensee. No license shall be transferable, except as otherwise provided in this article. 
(b)  In case of the death of a licensee, the establishment shall be allowed to continue to sell alcoholic beverages for a period of 45 days from the date of death or until expiration of the license or until approval of a new licensee, whichever shall first occur. 
(c)  If a licensee severs his association with a licensed establishment, the establishment may continue to sell alcoholic beverages for a period of 45 days from the date determined to be the date of severance or until expiration of the license or until approval of a new licensee, which shall first occur. This section shall not apply, however, to the withdrawal of one or more partners licensees from a partnership in favor of one or more partners who were partners at the time of the issuance of the license. 
(d)  A license issued hereunder shall be revoked by operation of law whenever partners are added to a partnership who were not partners of the partnership at the time of the issuance of the license, members or managers of a limited liability company ("LLC") are added to the LLC who were not members or managers of the LLC at the time of the issuance of the license, or officers, directors, or majority shareholders are added to a corporation who were not officers, directors, or majority shareholders of the corporation at the time of the issuance of the license. 
(e)  No transfer of a license to a new location shall be permitted where such move is made other than as a result of the exercise of eminent domain. Any change which is a result of the exercise of eminent domain shall authorize the transfer of a license to a new location, provided that such location meets all the qualifying criteria for a location in an initial application. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-98. - License as privilege. 
Any license issued hereunder shall be a mere grant of the privilege, and not a right, to carry on such licensed business during the term of such license or permit, subject to compliance with all the terms and conditions imposed by this article, or imposed by any other ordinance, resolution, or code provision of the City of Milner, Georgia; and any such license shall be subject to revocation or suspension at any time or times by the governing authority of the city without the refund of any license fee paid by the licensee; and the violation of any provision of this article shall be grounds for immediate revocation or suspension of any license or permit issued hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-99. - Revocation by state. 
Whenever the state shall revoke any license of any licensee to sell at wholesale or retail any alcoholic beverages, the city license to sell alcoholic beverages shall thereupon be automatically revoked without any action by the city council or any city officer. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-100. - Revocation by city. 
The city council may suspend or revoke a license issued hereunder upon a finding after a hearing before the city council that the licensee, or the licensee's agent or employee, acting within the scope of his employment, violated any provision of this article or violated any law, state or federal, pertaining to the conduct of the licensee's business. The city shall give the licensee at least three days' written notice of a hearing conducted pursuant to this section. Hearings under this section shall be transcribed by a court reporter, whose services shall be paid for by the licensee. The licensee shall have the right to cross-examine witnesses. After hearing the evidence, the city council shall decide by majority vote whether a license should be suspended or revoked. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Sec. 22-101. - No refund of fee upon revocation. 
Where a license issued hereunder is revoked pursuant to any provision of this article, the licensee shall not be entitled to any refund of license fees. 
(Ord. No. 08-5, § 2, 6-11-2008) 
Secs. 22-102—22-129. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - BEER AND WINE SALES FOR CONSUMPTION ON THE PREMISES 

Sec. 22-130. - Definitions. 
The following terms and words are hereby defined and shall be interpreted, as follows: 
Beer shall mean any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other similar product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six percent alcohol by volume and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, small beer, and strong beer. The word does not include sake, known as Japanese rice wine. The term "beer" shall be synonymous with "malt beverage." 
City shall mean the City of Milner, Georgia. 
Commercial district shall mean any zoning district in the city starting with the letter "C". 
Corporation shall include both "S" corporation and "C" corporations. 
Licensee shall mean the individual to whom a license is issued or, in the case of a partnership or corporation, all partners of the partnership and all officers and directors of the corporation. 
On-premises consumption retail beer dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that engages in selling or handling of beer, as hereinabove defined, at retail for consumption on the licensee's premises within the city. 
On-premises consumption retail wine dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that engages in selling or handling of wine, as hereinafter defined, at retail for consumption on the licensee's premises within the city. 
Partnership shall include a general partnership, limited partnership, limited liability partnership, and limited liability limited partnership. 
Premises shall mean the building described in the application for a license issued hereunder to any licensee; provided, however, this definition shall not include the property or grounds upon which said building is located. 
Restaurant shall mean any public place kept, used, maintained, advertised and held out to the public as a place where meals are served, and where meals are actually and regularly served, without sleeping accommodations, such place being provided with adequate and sanitary kitchen and dining room equipment and a seating capacity for at least 40 people, having employed therein a sufficient number and kind of employees to prepare, cook and serve suitable food to its customers. At least one meal per day shall be served at least five days a week, with the exception of holidays, and the serving of such meals shall be the principal business conducted on the licensee's premises, with the sale of any beer and/or wine for consumption on the premises, only being incidental thereto; provided further that beer and wine shall be sold only in conjunction with the serving of food. 
Wholesale beer dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that sells and/or deals in beer, as hereinabove defined, to an on-premises consumption retail beer dealer, as hereinabove defined, to or within the city. 
Wholesale wine dealer shall mean and include every person, firm, corporation or association that sells and/or deals in wine, as hereinabove defined, to an on-premises consumption retail wine dealer, as hereinafter defined, to or within the city. 
Wine shall mean any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines, and like products. The term does not include cooking wine mixed with sale or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to the definition of wine contained in hereinabove. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-100), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-131. - Requirement of license. 
Beer and wine may be sold or distributed in the city only under a license granted by the city, upon the terms and conditions provided in this article. In addition to these licenses identified in chapter 22, section 22-77, the city is empowered to grant the following classes of licenses: 
(1)  License for the retail sale of beer for on-premises consumption; 
(2)  License for the retail sale of wine for on-premises consumption. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-101), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-132. - Application for sale or distribution. 
All persons desiring to sell beer and/or wine shall make application on the forms prescribed by the city. The content of all applications shall be sworn to by the applicant before a notary public or other officer qualified to administer oaths. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-102), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-133. - Location requirements. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person unless the premises of the proposed location is situated: 
(1)  300 feet or more from the property line of any church, synagogue, shrine, or other place used exclusively for religious services, including the chapel of a mortuary or cemetery; 
(2)  300 feet or more from the property line of any school ground or college campus. The schools and colleges referred to herein shall include only such state, county, city, church, or other schools as teach the subjects commonly taught in the common schools and colleges of this state, and shall not include schools or colleges wherein only specialized subjects such as law, stenography, business, music, art, medicine, dentistry, vocational occupations, karate and other martial arts, performing arts, and other special subjects are taught; 
(3)  100 feet or more from the property line of any private residence, unless such residence is itself in a commercial district; 
(4)  100 feet or more from the property line of an alcoholic treatment center; and 
(5)  100 feet or more from the property line of any branch of any public library. 
(6)  For purposes of this section, distances shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-103), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-134. - Location limited to commercial district. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to any person unless the premises of the proposed location is situated in a commercially zoning district. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-104), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-135. - Visibility of entrance. 
No license shall be granted hereunder to an on-premises consumption retail beer dealer or an on-premises consumption retail wine dealer unless the front entrance to the premises is clearly visible from a public street. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-105), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-136. - Package sales prohibited. 
No alcoholic beverages may be sold by the package from the premises licensed for the sale of beer and wine for on-premises consumption; provided that this provision shall not prohibit the serving of a single can or bottle of beer or wine to any patron for consumption on the premises where such sale is otherwise lawful. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-106), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-137. - Removal of beverages prohibited. 
All beer and wine sold by a licensee hereunder shall be consumed only on the licensed premises. It shall be unlawful for any person to purchase beer and wine on the licensed premises and remove them. Each licensee shall be responsible for ensuring that no person who purchases beer and wine removes them from the premises in any manner. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-107), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-138. - Retail sales permitted in restaurants; minimum percentage of nonalcoholic sales. 
Any license granted to any on-premises consumption retail beer dealer or on-premises consumption retail wine dealer shall be for on-premises consumption which derives at least 51 percent of its total annual gross sales from the sale of food prepared on the premises and nonalcoholic beverages consumed on the premises. It shall be the responsibility of the licensee to ensure that this requirement is met on an annual basis and to maintain all records necessary for a validation thereof by designated city officials. A licensee's failure to maintain the required sales ratio shall constitute grounds for the revocation of such license. The city shall have the right, upon reasonable notice, to inspect licensee's records and books for the purpose of determining compliance with this section. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-108), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-139. - Filing reports. 
Each licensee shall file with the city manager a copy of the licensee's monthly state sales tax report as filed with the state department of revenue. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-109), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-140. - Sales audit. 
In addition to the reporting requirements detailed in sections 22-108 and 22-109, each licensee shall annually furnish to the city manager a statement from a certified public accountant that reports the percentage of the licensee's total sales derived from the sale of food and nonalcoholic beverages sold on the premises compared to the sale of all alcoholic beverages sold on the premises for the preceding year. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-110), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-141. - Serving of standing customers at bars prohibited. 
No licensee may serve any customer who is not seated at a table, provided that nothing shall prohibit being served while standing at a bar or counter where beer and/or wine is sold in conjunction with the serving of food. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-111), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-142. - Age/criminal record of applicant. 
Any applicant for a license under this ordinance shall be 25 years of age or older, an American citizen or an alien lawfully admitted for permanent residence, and have resided in the State of Georgia for a period of one year. No applicant shall have been convicted of, pled guilty to or pled nolo contendere to any felony or misdemeanor charge, other than traffic offenses, within ten years of the date of submission of the application, nor shall any such applicant have been incarcerated, on probation or on parole within five years preceding the date of submission of the application as a result of any felony conviction, plea of guilty or plea of nolo contendere. Where the applicant is a partnership or corporation, the requirements of this section shall apply to all of the applicant's partners, officers, directors, and majority shareholders. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-112), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-143. - Application contents. 
The license application shall include, but not be limited to, the name and address of the applicant; the proposed business location; the type of business to be conducted; if a partnership, the names and residence addresses of the partners; and if a corporation, the names of the directors, officers, and shareholders, the name and address of the corporation's agent for service of process, and the name and address of any other person or entity having a financial interest in the entity which is to own or operate the establishment for which a license is sought. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-113), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-144. - Surveyor certification. 
All original applications for new licenses shall include a certificate from a registered surveyor showing a scale drawing of the location of the proposed or existing premises, and stating both the straight line distance and the distance measured along the closest and most reasonable public access from the proposed or existing premises to the building and property line of the nearest church, school, library, alcoholic treatment center, and private residence. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-114), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-145. - Compliance of new commercial structure required. 
Where a building intended for the sale of beer and/or wine is at the time of the application for such license not in existence or not yet completed, a license may be issued for such location, provided the plans for the proposed building show clear compliance with all provisions of this article and applicable provisions of the City Code. No sales shall be allowed in such establishment, however, until it has been completed in accordance with such plans. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-115), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-146. - Application fee. 
Each application for an on-premises consumption retail beer dealer license or an on-premises consumption retail wine dealer license shall be accompanied by a nonrefundable application fee in the amount of $250.00. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-116), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-147. - State license required. 
A wholesale beer dealer license or wholesale wine dealer license shall be issued only to those persons who are licensed by the State of Georgia to sell and distribute beer or wine or both, as a wholesale dealer of such products. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-117), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-148. - Fingerprints. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 3-3-2(c), each license application shall be accompanied by a complete set of the applicant's fingerprints. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-118), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-149. - Investigation of applicant/applicant consent thereto. 
After receipt of an application in proper form, the city shall direct an investigation to verify the contents of the application and ensure conformance with the provisions of this article. The applicant shall be given written notice of any additional data which may be required to facilitate or complete the verification process. The city manager shall prepare or direct the preparation of a report and recommendation and deliver same to the city council for its consideration. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-119), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-150. - Procedure for approval. 
After all procedures called for under this ordinance have been completed, the application shall be administratively reviewed by the city council. If it is determined that the applicant meets all standards and requirements of this article, then the license applied for shall be granted upon payment of the applicable license fee(s), unless some specific cause related to location, traffic condition, or other environmental condition shall justify refusal, and the city shall deliver by mail to the applicant a writing evidencing such approval. If it is determined that the application fails to meet all standards and requirements of this article, it shall be rejected and the applicant shall be notified by mail of the rejection stating the reasons therefore. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-120), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-151. - Issuance of license to corporation. 
Where an applicant is a corporation, the license shall be issued jointly to the corporation and to the majority shareholder, if an individual. Where the majority shareholder is not an individual, the license shall be issued jointly to the corporation and its president, as evidenced in the corporation's articles of incorporation. Where an applicant is a limited liability company, the license shall be issued to one of the company's members or managers. Where an applicant is a partnership, the license shall be issued to one of the partners, if an individual. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-121), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-152. - Corporation registered agent in city required. 
All licensees that are corporations shall have and continuously maintain in the city a registered agent upon whom any required process and/or notice may be served. The licensee shall file the name of such agent along with the written consent of such agent with the city manager. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-122), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-153. - Request for hearing. 
Within 30 days of the city council's written decision to deny an application under this article, the applicant may file a request for a hearing before the city council to present evidence and cross-examine opposing witnesses. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-123), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-154. - Restriction on submittal of subsequent applications. 
An unsuccessful applicant for a license under this article may not submit a new application for the same location for 12 months after the date of the original application. An unsuccessful applicant may submit a new application for a different location at any time after final rejection of the prior application. No applicant shall have more than one application outstanding at the same time. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-124), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-155. - Annual license fees. 
All licenses issued shall be for the calendar year, and shall be paid in accordance with the following provisions: 
(1)  The fee for an on-premises consumption retail beer dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for an on-premises consumption retail beer dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(2)  The fee for a wholesale beer dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $100.00. The prorated fee for a wholesale beer dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $75.00. 
(3)  The fee for an on-premises consumption retail wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $500.00. The prorated fee for an on-premises consumption retail wine deal license issued after July 1 shall be $300.00. 
(4)  The fee for a wholesale wine dealer license issued prior to or on July 1 shall be $1,000.00. The prorated fee for a wholesale wine dealer license issued after July 1 shall be $600.00. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-125), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-156. - License expiration. 
All licenses issued hereunder shall expire at midnight on December 31 of each year unless renewed as hereinafter provided. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-126), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-157. - Renewal application. 
(a)  Licensees who desire to renew their licenses shall file an application and submit the requisite license fees to the city manager on the form prescribed by the city manager. Applications for renewal shall be filed before December 1 of each year. Renewal applications shall be reviewed by the city manager and upon investigation if there is no change in the ownership of licensee and no adverse reports from those agencies or departments required to inspect the premises of the licensee, the city manager shall issue a renewal license for the ensuing year, upon payment of the applicable license fee(s); and 
(b)  No new or renewal licenses shall be issued to any applicant who is delinquent in the payment of city taxes or fees, including, but not limited to, property taxes, alcoholic beverage excise taxes as hereinafter set forth, business license fees, or any other taxes or fees which are owed to the city by the applicant. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-127), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-158. - Excise tax. 
(a)  There is hereby imposed upon and levied against every licensed wholesale beer dealer an excise tax, in addition to the excise taxes levied by the state, as follows: 
(1)  Where malt beverages, commonly known as tap or draft beer, are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a tax of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more than 15½ gallons, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 15½ gallons; 
(2)  Where malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
(b)  The excise tax levied and imposed in this section is levied and imposed with respect to malt beverages sold or distributed by such wholesalers in the city to retailers doing business in the city. The excise tax provided for in this section shall be paid by such licensed wholesale dealers to the city on or before the tenth day of the month following the calendar month in which the beverages are sold or disposed of by such licensed wholesale dealer. Every licensee responsible for the payment of the excise tax imposed by this section shall file a report with the city itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of malt beverages, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. 
(c)  There is hereby imposed upon and levied against every licensed wholesale wine dealer an excise tax, in addition to the excise taxes levied by the state, a tax of $0.22 per liter, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(d)  The excise tax levied and imposed in this section is levied and imposed with respect to wine sold or distributed by such wholesalers in the city to retailers doing business in the city. The excise tax provided for in this section shall be paid by such licensed wholesale dealers to the city on or before the tenth day of the month following the calendar month in which the wine is sold or disposed of by such licensed wholesale dealer. Every licensee responsible for the payment of the excise tax imposed by this section shall file a report with the city manager itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of wine, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-128), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-159. - Hours of sale and/or delivery. 
(a)  On-premises consumption retail beer dealers and on-premises consumption retail wine dealers shall not engage in the sale of beer and/or wine except between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 11:45 p.m., Monday through Saturday; 
(b)  There shall be no sale of alcoholic beverages on Sunday; 
(c)  It shall be unlawful to make wholesale deliveries of beer and/or wine except between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 p.m., Monday through Saturday; and 
(d)  The retail sale of beer and/or wine is authorized on any election days. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-129), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-160. - "Happy hour" promotions. 
It is the intent of the section to prohibit activities typically associated with promotions referred to as "happy hour." No licensee under this chapter, or employee or agent of a licensee shall engage in any of the following practices in connection with the sale or other disposition of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises: 
(1)  The giving away of any alcoholic beverage in conjunction with the sale of any other alcoholic beverage; 
(2)  The sale of two or more alcoholic beverages for a single price, including the sale of all such beverages a customer can or desires to drink at a single price; 
(3)  Selling, offering to sell, or delivering to any person or persons any alcoholic beverage at a price less than one-half the price customarily charged for such alcoholic beverage, provided nothing contained herein shall be construed to prohibit the permanent reduction of the price of a drink or drinks up to one-half the price customarily charged; 
(4)  Requiring or encouraging the purchase of a second or subsequent alcoholic beverage at the same time another such beverage is purchased or before the first beverage has been consumed by any one person; 
(5)  Increasing the volume of alcoholic beverage contained in a drink without proportionately increasing the price customarily charged for such beverage; or 
(6)  Sponsoring, conducting, or allowing contests or promotions which have as their primary purpose the increasing of the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-130), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-161. - Limitation on signage. 
No sign of any kind, painted or electronic, advertising any price of beer or wine shall be permitted on the exterior of any licensed premises. No placard or sign of any kind which is visible from the exterior of the licensed premises shall make reference to the price of any beer or wine sold therein. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-131), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-162. - Limitation on license transfer. 
(a)  All licenses issued hereunder shall be personal to the licensee. No license shall be transferable, except as otherwise provided in this article. 
(b)  In case of the death of a licensee, the establishment shall be allowed to continue to sell alcoholic beverages for a period of 45 days from the date of death or until expiration of the license or until approval of a new licensee, whichever shall first occur. 
(c)  If a licensee severs his association with a licensed establishment, the establishment may continue to sell alcoholic beverages for a period of 45 days from the date determined to be the date of severance or until expiration of the license or until approval of a new licensee, which shall first occur. This section shall not apply, however, to the withdrawal of one or more partners licensees from a partnership in favor of one or more partners who were partners at the time of the issuance of the license. 
(d)  A license issued hereunder shall be revoked by operation of law whenever partners are added to a partnership who were not partners of the partnership at the time of the issuance of the license, members or managers of a limited liability company ("LLC") are added to the LLC who were not members or managers of the LLC at the time of the issuance of the license, or officers, directors, or majority shareholders are added to a corporation who were not officers, directors, or majority shareholders of the corporation at the time of the issuance of the license. 
(e)  No transfer of a license to a new location shall be permitted where such move is made other than as a result of the exercise of eminent domain. Any change which is a result of the exercise of eminent domain shall authorize the transfer of a license to a new location, provided that such location meets all the qualifying criteria for a location in an initial application. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-132), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-163. - License as privilege. 
Any license issued hereunder shall be a mere grant of the privilege, and not a right, to carry on such licensed business during the term of such license or permit, subject to compliance with all the terms and conditions imposed by this article, or imposed by any other ordinance, resolution, of code provision of the City of Milner, Georgia; and any such license shall be subject to revocation or suspension at any time or times by the governing authority of the city without the refund of any license fee paid by the licensee; and the violation of any provision of this article shall be grounds for immediate revocation or suspension of any license or permit issued hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(21-34), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-164. - Revocation by state. 
Whenever the state shall revoke any license of any licensee to sell at wholesale or retail any alcoholic beverages, the city license to sell alcoholic beverages shall thereupon be automatically revoked without any action by the city council or any city officer. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-133), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-165. - Revocation by city. 
The city council may suspend or revoke a license issued hereunder upon a finding after a hearing before the city council that the licensee, or the licensee's agent or employee, acting within the scope of his employment, violated any provision of this article or violated any law, state or federal, pertaining to the conduct of the licensee's business. The city shall give the licensee at least three days written notice of a hearing conducted pursuant to this section. Hearings under this section shall be transcribed by a court reporter, whose services shall be paid for by the licensee. The licensee shall have the right to cross-examine witnesses. After hearing the evidence, the city council shall decide by majority vote whether a license should be suspended or revoked. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-134), 3-18-2009) 
Sec. 22-166. - No refund of fee upon revocation. 
Where a license issued hereunder is revoked pursuant to any provision of this article, the licensee shall not be entitled to any refund of license fees. 
(Ord. No. 09-1, § 2(22-135), 3-18-2009) 
Secs. 22-167—22-189. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - TELEPHONE AND TELEGRAPH FRANCHISE FEES 

Sec. 22-190. - Application for placement of lines and facilities in the right-of-way. 
(a)  Any telegraph or telephone company that places or seeks to place lines and facilities in the public roads, highways or rights-of-way shall provide to the city the following information, in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1(b)(1): 
(1)  The name, address, and telephone number of a principal office and local agent of such telegraph or telephone company; 
(2)  Proof of certification from the Georgia Public Service Commission of such telegraph or telephone company to provide telecommunications services in this state; 
(3)  Proof of insurance or self-insurance of such telegraph or telephone company adequate to defend and cover claims of third parties and of city authorities; 
(4)  A description of the telegraph or telephone company's service area, which description shall be sufficiently detailed so as to allow the city to respond to subscriber inquiries. For the purposes of this section, a telegraph or telephone company may, in lieu of or as supplement to a written description, provide a map on 8½ by 11 inch paper that is clear and legible and that fairly depicts the service area within the boundaries of the city. If such service area is less than the boundaries of the city, the map shall describe the boundaries of the geographic area to be served in clear and concise terms; 
(5)  A description of the services to be provided; 
(6)  An affirmative declaration that the telegraph or telephone company shall comply with all applicable federal, state, and local laws and regulations, including city ordinances and regulations, regarding the placement and maintenance of facilities in the public rights of way that are reasonable, nondiscriminatory, and applicable to all users of the public rights-of-way, including the requirements of O.C.G.A. tit. 25, ch. 9, the "Georgia Utility Facility Protection Act"; and 
(7)  A statement in bold type at the top of the application as follows: "Pursuant to paragraph (2) of subsection (b) of Code Section 46-5-1 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated, the city shall notify the applicant of any deficiencies in this application within 15 business days of receipt of this application." 
(b)  The city shall notify the telegraph or telephone company within 15 business days of the receipt of any application deemed incomplete; such notice shall specifically identify all application deficiencies. If no such notification is given within 15 business days of the receipt of an application, such application shall be deemed complete. 
(c)  Within 60 calendar days of the receipt of a completed application, the city may adopt such application by adoption of a resolution or ordinance or by notification to the telegraph or telephone company. The failure of the city to adopt an application within 60 calendar days of the receipt of a completed application shall constitute final adoption of such application. 
(d)  If it modifies its service area or provisioned services identified in the original application, the telegraph or telephone company shall notify the city of changes to the service area or the services provided. Such notice shall be given at least 20 days prior to the effective date of such change. Such notification shall contain a geographic description of the new service area or areas and new services to be provided within the jurisdiction of the city, if any. The city shall provide to all telegraph and telephone companies located in its rights-of-way written notice of annexations and changes in the city's corporate boundaries which, for the purposes of this Code section, shall become effective 30 days following receipt. 
(e)  An application adopted pursuant to this section may be terminated by a telegraph or telephone company by submitting a notice of termination to the city. For purposes of this section, such notice shall identify the telegraph or telephone company, the affected service area, and the effective date of such termination, which shall not be less than 60 calendar days from the date of filing the notice of termination. 
(f)  Any telegraph or telephone company that has previously obtained permits for the placement of its facilities, has specified the name of such telegraph or telephone company in such permit application, has previously placed its facilities in any public right-of-way, and has paid and continues to pay any applicable city occupational license taxes, permit fees, franchise fees, except as set forth in subsection (h) or, if applicable, county permit fees shall be deemed to have complied with this section without any further action on the part of such telegraph or telephone company except as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1(b)(8), (9), (11), and (17). 
(g)  Noncompliance. 
(1)  Any telegraph or telephone company that has placed lines and facilities in the public roads and highways or rights of way of the city without first obtaining permits or otherwise notifying the city of its presence in the public roads and highways or rights-of-way shall provide the information required by paragraph (a) of this subsection, if applicable, to the city on or before the expiration of 90 days from the effective date of this article. 
(2)  After the expiration of 90 days from the effective date of this article, if any telegraph or telephone company, other than those who meet the requirements of paragraph (f) of this subsection, has failed or fails to provide the information required by paragraph (a) of this subsection to the city, the city shall provide written notice to such telegraph or telephone company giving that company 15 calendar days from the date of receipt of such notice to comply with this section. 
(3)  In the event the 15-calendar-day cure period expires without compliance, the city may petition the Georgia Public Service Commission which shall, after an opportunity for a hearing, order the appropriate relief. 
(h)  Existing franchise agreement. 
(1)  In the event any telegraph or telephone company has an existing, valid city franchise agreement as of the effective date of this article, the terms and conditions of such existing franchise agreement shall only remain effective and enforceable until the expiration of the existing agreement or December 31, 2012, whichever shall first occur. 
(2)  In the event any telegraph or telephone company is paying an existing occupational license tax or fee, based on actual recurring local services revenues, as of the effective date of this article, such payment shall be considered the payment of due compensation without further action on the part of the city. 
(3)  In the event that the rate of such existing tax or fee exceeds three percent of actual recurring local service revenues, that rate shall remain effective until December 31, 2012; thereafter, the payment by such telegraph or telephone company at the rate of three percent shall be considered the payment of due compensation without further action on the part of the city. 
(Ord. No. 10-4, § 1(22-61), 10-13-2010) 
Sec. 22-191. - Due compensation for telephone companies with end user retail customers within the city. 
(a)  The city hereby requires due compensation of three percent of actual recurring local service revenues, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1(b)(8) and (9); provided, however, that any company which pays in excess of three percent of actual recurring local service revenues pursuant to an existing franchise agreement shall continue to pay in accordance with the agreement until the expiration of the franchise agreement or December 31, 2012, whichever occurs first; and any company which pays in excess of three percent of actual recurring local service revenues in accordance with an occupational license tax arrangement shall continue to pay in accordance with such payment schedule until December 31, 2012. 
(b)  Regarding any telephone company that does not have retail, end user customers located within the city's corporate boundaries, the payment by such company to city in accordance with the rates set by regulations promulgated by the department of transportation for the use of its rights of way shall be considered the payment of due compensation. 
(c)  Any due compensation paid in accordance with this section shall be in lieu of any other permit fee in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1(b)(10). 
(d)  The city hereby incorporates the calculation of "due compensation" assessment upon retail, end user customers, and notice of nonpayment provisions codified in O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1. 
(Ord. No. 10-4, § 1(22-62), 10-13-2010) 
Sec. 22-192. - Actual recurring local service revenues. 
(a)  "Recurring local service revenues", as defined by O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1, means those revenues customarily included in the uniform system of accounts as prescribed by the Federal Communications Commission for class "A" and "B" companies; provided, however, that only the local service portion of the following accounts shall be included, for example: 
(1)  Basic local service revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5000; 
(2)  Basic area revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5001; 
(3)  Optional extended area revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 2.5002; 
(4)  Public telephone revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5010; 
(5)  Local private line revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 35.5040; provided, however, that the portion of such accounts attributable to audio and video program transmission service where both terminals of the private line are within the corporate limits of the city shall not be included; 
(6)  Other local exchange revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5060; 
(7)  Local exchange service, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5069; 
(8)  Network access revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5080; 
(9)  Directory revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5320; provided, however, that the portion of such accounts attributable to revenue derived from listings in portion of directories not considered white pages shall not be included; 
(10)  Nonregulated operating revenue, as defined in 47 C.F.R. § 32.5280; provided, however, that the portion of such accounts attributable to revenues derived from private lines shall not be included; and 
(11)  Uncollectible revenue, as defined in 47 § C.F.R. 32.5300. 
(Ord. No. 10-4, § 1(22-63), 10-13-2010) 
Sec. 22-193. - Authorized designee. 
The city clerk shall, on behalf of the city, exercise day-to-day administrative duties necessary to fulfill the regulatory authority of the city under O.C.G.A. § 46-5-1 et seq., and shall perform the following duties: 
(1)  Review application information submitted by a telephone company to the city and, if an application is incomplete, notify the telegraph or telephone company within 15 business days of the receipt of such application, identifying in such notice all application deficiencies. 
(2)  Report the receipt of a completed application to the city council within 60 calendar days of the receipt of such completed application. 
(3)  Review payments of due compensation submitted by the company to ensure compliance with the provisions of the amended law and this article. 
(4)  Provide a coordination function between a telephone company and all city departments on any matter relating to the amended law and this article. 
(5)  Arrange and evaluate, no more than once a year, a comprehensive review of the records of a company which is reasonably related to the calculation and payment of due compensation. 
(6)  Provide to all telegraph and telephone companies located in its rights-of-way written notice of annexations and changes in the city's corporate boundaries. 
(Ord. No. 10-4, § 1(22-64), 10-13-2010) 
Secs. 22-194—22-200. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - BODY ART RULES AND REGULATIONS 

Sec. 22-201. - Body art rules and regulations. 
The rules and regulations for body art studios and body artists adopted by the Lamar County Board of Health, as amended, are incorporated herein by reference and made a part of this article as if fully rewritten herein. Said rules and regulations shall be enforced by the City of Milner, and any violations thereof may be tried in the municipal court of the city or any other court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. No. 13-2, § 1, 11-14-2013) 
Secs. 22-202—22-210. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - ADULT ENTERTAINMENT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 22-211. - Findings; public purpose. 
(a)  It is the finding of the mayor and council that public nudity (either partial or total) under certain circumstances, particularly circumstances related to the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages in so-called nude bars or establishments offering so-called nude entertainment or adult entertainment, leads to an increase in the surrounding area of criminal behavior and creates undesirable community conditions, blight and diminution in property values. 
(b)  Among the acts of criminal behavior identified with the commercial combination of live nudity and alcohol, and live commercial nudity in general, are disorderly conduct, prostitution, solicitation, drug trafficking, drug use and corruption of public officials. Among the undesirable community conditions identified with the commercial combination of live nudity and alcohol, and commercial nudity in general, are depression of property values and acceleration of community blight in the surrounding neighborhood, increased allocation of and expenditure for law enforcement personnel to preserve law and order, and increased burden on the judicial system as a consequence of the criminal behavior hereinabove described. 
(c)  Accordingly, it is in the best interests of the health, welfare, safety and morals of the community to reduce the adverse impact of adult entertainment establishments by limiting the number of such uses, so as to reduce the negative impacts of adult entertainment establishments upon other business uses, neighborhood property values, residential areas and public and semi-public uses; to insure that adult entertainment establishments do not impede development, redevelopment and neighborhood revitalization efforts; and so as to avoid allowing adult entertainment establishments in heavily used public pedestrian areas. 
(d)  Therefore, the limitation of adult entertainment to certain prescribed areas of the city is in the public welfare, and it is a matter of governmental interest and concern to minimize the occurrence of criminal behavior and undesirable community conditions normally associated with establishments which provide or establish adult entertainment. 
(Ord. No. 14-1, § 1, 6-11-2014) 
Sec. 22-212. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Adult bookstore means an establishment having a substantial or significant portion of its stock in trade, books, magazines or other periodicals which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas or an establishment with a segment or section, comprising five percent of its total floor space, devoted to the sale or display of such materials or five percent of its net sales consisting of printed materials which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
Adult dancing establishment means a business that features live dancers on the premises engaged in displaying or exposing specified anatomical areas. 
Adult entertainment establishments shall mean and include adult dancing establishments, exotic dance establishments, adult bookstore, adult motion picture theaters, adult motion picture arcades, and adult video stores. 
Adult motion picture arcade means any place to which the public is permitted or invited wherein coins or slug-operated or electronically, electrically or mechanically controlled still or motion picture machines, projectors or other image-producing devices are maintained to show images to five or fewer persons per machine at any one time and where the images so displayed are distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on depicting or describing specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
Adult motion picture theater means an enclosed building used for presenting motion pictures distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas for observation by patrons therein. 
Adult video store means an establishment having a substantial or significant portion of its stock in trade, video tapes, DVDs or movies or other reproductions, whether for sale or rent, which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas or an establishment with a segment or section, comprising five percent of its total floor space, devoted to the sale or display of such material or which derives more than five percent of its net sales from videos which are characterized or distinguished by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas. 
Exotic dance establishment means a nightclub, theater or other establishment which features live performances on the premises by topless and/or bottomless dancers, go-go dancers, strippers or similar entertainers, where such performances are distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on specified sexual activities or by exposure of specified anatomical areas. 
Specified anatomical areas shall include any of the following: pubic hair, anus, vulva or genitals of either males or females, or any portion of the areola of the female breast. 
Specified sexual activities means and shall include any of the following: 
(1)  Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory functions in the context of a sexual relationship and any of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct: anilingus, buggery, coprophagy, coprophilia, cunnilingus, fellatio, necrophilia, pederasty, pedophilia, piquerism, sapphism, zooerasty. 
(2)  Clearly depicted human genitals, in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence. 
(3)  Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, oral copulation, coitus or masturbation. 
(4)  Fondling or touching of nude human genitals, pubic region, buttocks or female breast. 
(5)  Masochism, erotic or sexually oriented torture, beating or the infliction of pain. 
(6)  Erotic or lewd touching, fondling or other sexual contact with an animal by a human being. 
(7)  Human excretion, urination, menstruation, vaginal or anal irrigation. 
(Ord. No. 14-1, § 1, 6-11-2014) 
Sec. 22-213. - Violations; penalty. 
(a)  Any person violating the provisions of this article shall be guilty of an offense punishable as provided in section 4.13 of the City Charter. 
(b)  In addition to fine or imprisonment, violation of this article shall be grounds for suspension or revocation of the license issued under this article. 
(c)  Any person who holds an adult entertainment establishment license must also comply with all applicable local, state and federal laws or regulations otherwise pertaining to these establishments, and failure to so comply shall be grounds for suspension or revocation of the license issued under this article. 
(Ord. No. 14-1, § 1, 6-11-2014) 
Sec. 22-214. - Unlawful operation declared nuisance. 
Any adult entertainment establishment operated, conducted or maintained contrary to the provisions of this article shall be and the same is hereby declared to be unlawful and a public nuisance. The city may, in addition to or in lieu of prosecuting a criminal action under this article, commence an action or actions, proceeding or proceedings, for abatement, removal or enjoinment thereof in the manner provided by law. It shall take such other steps and shall apply to such court or courts as may have jurisdiction to grant such relief as will abate or remove such adult entertainment establishment and restrain and enjoin any person from operating, conducting or maintaining an adult entertainment establishment contrary to the provisions of this article.
