Whenever screening is required by this chapter or as a condition of zoning imposed by the mayor and council, a durable masonry wall, or fence or hedge of sufficient opacity to provide a visual blind designed to be compatible with the character of adjoining properties, shall be provided. Such wall or fence shall be at least six feet in height, but no greater than eight feet in height, measured from the ground along the common lot lines of the adjoining properties. When hedges or natural plantings are used, together with the fence prescribed, to form the required screening, the minimum sufficient opacity shall be deemed to require no less than three feet of plantings and/or hedge in the area immediately adjacent to the fence, measured along the ground surface from the fence to the inside border of said plantings and/or hedge. Such plantings must be in place prior to the issuance of a building permit for any improvements. Hedges and plantings shall be of such variety that an average height of at least six feet could be expected by normal growth within no later than two years from the time of planting. 
(Ord. No. 2007-8, § 2, 3-21-2007) 
Secs. 118-403—118-419. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - COMMERCIAL/INDUSTRIAL DEVELOPMENT ORDINANCE OF THE CITY OF MILNER, GEORGIA 
DIVISION 1. - JURISDICTION AND PURPOSE 

Sec. 118-420. - Short title. 
This article shall be known as the Commercial/Industrial Development Ordinance of the City of Milner, Georgia. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(101), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-421. - Authority. 
The power of the City of Milner to enact an ordinance governing the development standards for commercial and industrial development within its municipal city limits is set forth in the 1983 Constitution of the State of Georgia, Article 9, Section 2, Paragraph 4. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(102), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-422. - Jurisdiction. 
This article shall apply to all land within the City of Milner. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(103), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-423. - Purposes. 
This article seeks to encourage the development of desirable land use patterns within the City of Milner, the promotion of which is intended to reduce or eliminate the occurrence of conditions which can threaten the general health, safety and welfare of the residents of the City of Milner. This article promotes the following purposes: 
(1)  Encourage the development of the City of Milner as an economically sound and stable community; 
(2)  Assure the provision of required utilities, facilities and services to new land development within the City of Milner; 
(3)  Assure the redevelopment of the commercial areas located in or near the downtown of the City of Milner in a manner consistent with the historic character and architecture of the area; 
(4)  Assure the provision of needed public open spaces and building sites in new land development through the dedication or reservation of land for recreational, educational and other purposes; 
(5)  Assure the wise development of new areas in harmony with the City of Milner's Comprehensive Plan; 
(6)  Assure consideration of any environmental impact (past, present and future) as a result of new land development or redevelopment of already developed areas; and 
(7)  Assure site environmental inspection, clean-up and certification. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(104), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-424—118-439. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - DEFINITIONS 

Sec. 118-440. - Interpretation of common terms. 
When used in this article, the following words and phrases have the meaning as defined in this article. Terms not defined here have the same meaning as is found in most dictionaries, where consistent with the context of this article. The terms "must," "will" and "shall" are mandatory in nature, indicating that an action has to be done. The term "may" is permissive and allows discretion regarding an action. When consistent with the context, words used in the singular number include the plural, and those used in the plural include the singular. Words used in the present tense include the future. The word "developer" includes a firm, corporation, copartnership, association, joint venture, institution or person. The word "lot" includes the words "plot" and "parcel". The word "building" includes the word "structure." The words "used" or "occupied" as applied to any land or building include the words "intended, arranged or designed to be used or occupied." 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(201), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-441. - General definitions. 
Administrative officer means the city manager or such other individual or authorized representative designated by the mayor and council to be responsible for the enforcement of this article. 
Block means a piece or parcel of land entirely surrounded by public highways or streets, other than alleys. 
Buffer means that portion of a lot established for open space purposes and intended to separate properties with different and possibly incompatible types of use. A buffer shall not be occupied with structures and facilities, except as permitted by this article. Where required by this article, a buffer must include the installation of a suitable visual screen in accordance with the provisions of the City of Milner Zoning Ordinance. 
Building means any structure having a roof and intended for shelter, housing or enclosure of persons, animals or property of any kind. 
Building line means the line that represents the distance a building must be set back from the boundary line of a lot, measured at the foundation of the building. 
Building setback line means a line parallel to a specified minimum distance from the front, side or rear property lines beyond which no foundation wall or part of the structure of any building projects with the exception of roof overhang, steps and the subsurface projection of footings. 
Center line, street means that line surveyed and monumented by the governing authority, as the center line of a street or if such a center line has not been surveyed, it is the line running midway between the outside curbs or ditches of the street. 
City means the City of Milner, Georgia. 
Comprehensive plan means any part or element of the overall plan for development adopted by the mayor and council, as amended. 
Construction plan means a plan which shows all street design and profiles, topographic information, utility construction plans, sediment and erosion control plans and other information which may be required by the administrative officer. It is submitted to the administrative officer and requires only his approval after review by the appropriate city departments. 
Crosswalk means a right of way within a block dedicated to public use, intended primarily for pedestrian use and designated to provide access to adjacent roads and lots. 
Curb cut means the point at which vehicular access is provided to an adjoining street from a lot. 
Design standards means the specifications to land owners or developers for the preparation of plans indicating (among other things) the optimum, minimum or maximum dimensions of such characteristics as rights-of-way, setbacks, etc. 
Downtown development authority means the downtown development authority of the city, created pursuant to the provisions of state law governing such authorities. 
Downtown development authority overlay zone means that portion of the city bounded as follows: On the north by the intersection of Main Street and Liberty Hill Street; on the south by the intersection of Main Street and Garden Circle; on the east and west by a line a distance of 750 feet running parallel to the centerline of Main Street. This is the same area identified on a map designated as the downtown development authority overlay zone map. 
Easement means the right or privilege of using another's property, for purposes such as constructing and maintaining sanitary sewers, water mains, electric lines, telephone lines, storm sewers, gas lines, bicycle paths, pedestrian ways and other purposes. 
Elevation, front means the view of a building or group of buildings as seen from directly in front of the structure. 
Environmental matters means those matters pertaining to possible soil and groundwater contamination, including storage tanks, chemical use, storage and disposition of hazardous waste, solid waste disposal, air quality and surface water contamination. 
Flood boundary means that area threatened by possible flood under normal to severe circumstance; determined as shown on the flood insurance rate map, published by the Federal Emergency Management Agency. 
Lot means a parcel of land under single person or single entity ownership occupied or capable of being occupied by one or more buildings and customarily incidental accessory buildings or uses, including such open spaces as are required by this article. 
Lot, corner means a lot located at the intersection of two or more streets. 
Lot, double frontage means a lot, other than a corner lot, which has frontage on more than one street. 
Lot of record means a lot which is part of a subdivision, the plat of which has been recorded in the Office of the Clerk of Superior Court, Lamar County, Georgia, or a parcel of land described by metes and bounds, the plat or description of which has been recorded in said office. If a portion of a parcel has been conveyed at the time of the adoption of this article, the remaining portion of the lot or parcel will be considered a lot of record. 
Lot remnant means any portion or portions of a lot not suitable for building upon because of size or topography and remaining after the transfer of other portions of the lot to adjoining lots. 
Lot width means the distance between side lot lines measured at the front building line. If a corner lot, the distance between lot lines measured along the front building line that parallels or more nearly parallels the rear lot line. 
Owners of record means the owner(s) of property as specified on the deed of the lot of record. 
Parks and playgrounds means public or community land, open spaces or recreation areas represented on a subdivision plat as dedicated, reserved or intended to be reserved for recreational purposes. 
Pedestrian way means cross or other areas designed and marked specifically for pedestrian traffic. 
Percentage of grade means measured down the street centerline, the distance vertically (up and down) from the horizontal in feet and tenths of a foot for each 100 feet or horizontal distance. 
Planned development means a coordinated development designed and constructed according to a development plan which has been approved by the city. 
Planning commission means the planning commission of the city. 
Pre-application review means an initial and informal stage of review at which the developer may make known proposals and the city may respond and/or advise the developer concerning the application of the provisions of this article. 
Private drive means a nonpublic, privately owned accessway. 
Protective covenants means contracts made between private parties, or conditions recorded with an approved plat and running with the title to the land, specifying the manner in which land may be used, developed or improved with the intent of protecting and preserving the physical and economic integrity of a given area. 
Public hearing means an official session of the planning commission or mayor and council advertised according to law and called for purposes specified in the public notice. 
Reserve strip means a strip or parcel of land along, around or between properties for the purpose of restricting access. 
Review agency means any designated agency other than the planning commission or the mayor and council which may review appropriate parts of plan submissions by reason of technical capability, authority or interest. 
Right-of-way means a strip of land designed, reserved, dedicated or purchased for the purpose of pedestrian or vehicular access or utility line installation and owned by a county or municipality. 
Road means a public or private right-of-way affording primary access by pedestrians and vehicles to and between properties and designated as a street, highway, thoroughfare, parkway, road, avenue, boulevard or place. 
(1)  Alley or service drive means a minor accessway used for service access or property access under specified circumstances to the back or side of properties otherwise abutting a street. 
(2)  Cul-de-sac means a local street with only one outlet and having an appropriate terminal for the safe and convenient reversal of traffic movement. 
(3)  Road width means the shortest distance between lines of lots delineating the road right-of-way. 
(4)  Local street/road means a street used primarily for access to the abutting properties and to serve travel demands in the immediate area. For purposes of this chapter, a local street/road within the city shall be any street which is not designated as either a collector street/road and/or arterial street/road. 
(5)  Collector street/road : means a street which usually serves to either provide direct access to lots or distribute traffic from individual lots or distribute traffic from individual lots to major streets or arterials. It may also connect neighborhoods with one another. It should be designed to discourage excessive speeds and through traffic. 
(6)  Arterial street/road means a street which usually serves to either provide direct access to lots or distribute traffic from individual lots and collector streets through the city. It may also connect neighborhoods with one another. It should be designed to discourage excessive speeds and through traffic. For purposes of this chapter, the following streets within the city are designated as arterial: Main Street f/k/a Georgia Highway 41, US s41/GA7, Zebulon Street, Birch Street and Liberty Hill Street. 
(7)  Tangent means a straight line that is perpendicular to the radius of a curve where the tangent meets the curve. 
Subdivider means any individual, firm, association, syndicate, copartnership, corporation, trust or other legal entity having sufficient proprietary interest in the land sought to be subdivided to commence and maintain proceedings to subdivide the same under the provisions of this article. 
Subdivision means the division of a lot of record at the time of enactment of this article into three or more lots, building sites or other divisions for the purpose whether immediate or future of sale, legacy or building development. 
(1)  This definition includes all of the following: 
a.  All divisions of land involving a new street; 
b.  All divisions of land involving a change in existing streets; 
c.  Any resubdivision of land; 
d.  The process of subdividing; and 
e.  Any land or area subdivided. 
(2)  This definition does not include the following: 
a.  The combination or recombination of portions of previously platted lots where the total number of lots is not increased and the resultant lots are equal to the standards set forth in this chapter; 
b.  The transfer of property by the owner to a member of the immediate family (parent, spouse or child); 
c.  The transfer of unsubdivided land or the transfer of a lot or parcel of land established by deed or plat recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county prior to the initial effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived; 
d.  The division of land among heirs by judicial decree; and 
e.  The division of land into parcels of five or more acres where no new street is involved. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(202), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-442—118-449. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - FEES 

Sec. 118-450. - Fees. 
The following fees shall be assessed for submission, engineering cost, review and approval of construction plans for commercial/industrial development of real property. 
For developments consisting of: 
(1)  Less than 2 acres: As set by mayor and council. 
(2)  2—4.99 acres: As set by mayor and council. 
(3)  5—9.99 acres: As set by mayor and council. 
(4)  10 or more acres: As set by mayor and council. 
(5)  Additions to existing developments: As set by mayor and council. 
(6)  Utility installations: As set by mayor and council. 
(7)  Resubmittal of construction plans: As set by mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(301), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-451—118-459. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - GENERAL PROCEDURES 

Sec. 118-460. - Initial information. 
(a)  This division outlines procedures to be followed in order to comply with the requirements of this article. The developer, who initially may not be familiar with this article, must first consult with the administrative officer to obtain information concerning all ordinances affecting the proposed development. 
(b)  The administrative officer shall provide the developer with a copy of this article and any other ordinance governing the development. The developer may either review the article at city hall or he may purchase a copy for his subsequent use. 
(c)  The provisions of this article apply in addition to the provisions of the City Code of the City of Milner pertinent to subdivisions contained in section 114-1 et seq. In the event of a conflict between the two, the more stringent provision of either ordinance shall apply. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(401), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-461. - Required compliance with development regulations. 
(a)  Physical development. No developer may proceed with any construction work on a proposed development before obtaining construction plan approval and any and all required development permits. 
(b)  Use of plat. The transfer of, sale, agreement to sell, or negotiation to sell land by reference to, exhibition of, or other use of a plat that has not been given a final certificate of approval by the city and recorded in the Office of the Clerk of Superior Court of Lamar County is prohibited. The description by metes and bounds in the instrument of transfer or other documents does not exempt the transaction from this prohibition. 
(c)  Erection of building. No building permit will be issued, no building may be erected and no factory-manufactured building may be installed on any lot unless the street giving access to the lot has been approved in accordance with the provisions for the acceptance and dedication of streets by the city. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(402), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-462. - Overview of construction plan procedures. 
Prior to making any street improvements or installing any utilities or other improvements, the developer must submit to the administrative officer construction plans of the proposed development prepared in accordance with the provisions of this article. The construction plans must show all street design profiles, topographic information, utility construction plans, sediment and erosion control plans, and other information as may be requested by the administrative officer. The construction plan stage requires the review and approval of only the administrative officer and any appropriate city departments. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(403), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-463. - Submission and approval of construction plans. 
(a)  Construction plan submission. Prior to certification of zoning and issuance of a building permit, a site plan must be approved for all construction, including expansions and additions. 
(b)  Format. Nine copies of the construction plans must be submitted to the administrative officer. The scale shall not be less than 50 feet to the inch. 
(c)  Planned development. Development to be constructed in phases must have complete construction documents for all phases. 
(d)  Review of construction plans. The developer shall contact the following departments of the city for plan review, as follows: 
(1)  City fire department; 
(2)  City engineer; 
(3)  Lamar County Health Department; 
(4)  Towaliga Soil and Water Conservation Office; and 
(5)  Water/sewer department. 
These agencies must approve or disapprove the construction plans within 21 working days of receipt. If the plans are disapproved, the developer shall be notified in writing of the reason for disapproval. Upon receipt of the revised plans, all agencies shall approve or disapprove the revised construction plans within 21 days of receipt. When the plans are approved, the administrative officer is authorized to issue a permits to permit the developer to commence construction. 
(e)  Compliance with permit regulation for wetlands. The developer shall submit documents to show that the proposed construction complies with the terms and conditions of nationwide permit regulations, as promulgated by Part 330, Appendix (c)(13)(d) of Regulations for Wetlands published in the Federal Register, Volume 56, No. 226, November 22, 1991, as amended. 
(f)  Suitability of land. Land on which there is a danger to health, safety or property will not be approved for a use that will continue or increase such danger, unless such hazards can be and are corrected. Examples of such conditions are: 
(1)  Land subject to flooding, improper drainage or erosion; 
(2)  Land with excessive slope or other physical constraints which make it unsuitable for development. 
(g)  Approval of construction plans. Approval of construction plans and issuance of a building permit constitutes authorization to proceed with the installation of any required improvements, subject to the approval of agencies having the proper authority over such individual improvements. 
(h)  Approval period. Approval of construction plans is valid for a period of two years. Any application for a building permit submitted after that time has lapsed will not be accepted. Construction plans should be resubmitted and should conform to the current adopted standards (as of the date of resubmittal) of the city. Review fees will apply on resubmittal. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(404), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-464. - Specifications for construction plans. 
Construction plans must meet the minimum standards of design set forth in this section and must include the following: 
(1)  A letter requesting review and approval of the construction plans, giving the name, address and telephone number of the developer submitting the plan; 
(2)  Name and location of the development; 
(3)  Name, address, telephone number and seal of engineer preparing the plan; 
(4)  Vicinity map; 
(5)  Date, scale, north arrow and number of sheets; 
(6)  Zoning of property; 
(7)  Zoning of adjoining property; 
(8)  Location and dimensions of all existing structures (principal and accessory); 
(9)  Locations and dimensions of all proposed structures (principal and accessory) and proposed uses; 
(10)  Rights-of-way, pavement edges, centerlines of roadways and all easements; 
(11)  Minimum yards and setbacks specified in the zoning ordinance; 
(12)  Exits, entrances, internal circulation patterns showing traffic lanes, fire lanes and acceleration/deceleration lanes, and streets and driveways on both sides of the street within 100 feet of a property line; 
(13)  Parking layout, including handicapped parking and landscaping; 
(14)  Required landscape areas, buffers and screening; 
(15)  Off-street loading; 
(16)  Location of refuse collection and any outside storage and/or service areas, and how such refuse and storage areas will be screened; 
(17)  Signs; 
(18)  Field run or aerial topographic map referenced to a datum of mean sea level with contour intervals not to exceed two feet; 
(19)  Water and sanitary sewer plans (if applicable) which comply with all city sewer system standards; 
(20)  A specification chart on the plans with all pipe gauges and other pertinent specifications; 
(21)  Site grading plan with soil erosion and sedimentation control plan in accordance with the Towaliga Soil and Water Conservation District office standards; 
(22)  The 100-year floodplain must be depicted accurately and bear the certification of a registered professional engineer or professional surveyor and the sources of all data shall be identified on the plan. 
(23)  Hydrology study. 
a.  Hydrology study will be required for storm frequencies of two, five, ten, 25, 50 and 100 years. Studies shall include pertinent hydrographs, drainage maps, and outlet structures (plan and profile views). 
b.  Detention is required for storm frequencies of two, five, ten, 25 and 100 years. No additional runoff will be allowed over the predeveloped rate. All detention facilities shall be fenced with a cyclone fence a minimum of six feet in height. Potential access to detention facilities shall be provided by means of a 15-foot minimum width fence gate, latched and locked five or more feet above grade, a 15-foot minimum width easement to a public right-of-way. 
c.  Detention requirement for any development located adjacent to a watercourse with drainage basin significantly larger than the area proposed for development may include a required "timing study" analysis. If required, such study must comply with the guidelines set forth in the Georgia Stormwater Management Manual utilizing acceptable methods for determining flow path time and hydrographs. HEC-1 models must be utilized to produce hydrographs of the site and basin for use in determining peak flow rates at the study point determined to be the critical point of study. The ten percent rule outlined in the Georgia Stormwater Management Manual should be utilized in studying the downstream impact of development and reported in the study. A predesign meeting will be required before plans or a study is developed and submitted for review. 
(24)  Total area of the property; 
(25)  Area to be developed; 
(26)  Area of impervious surface; 
(27)  Percentage of impervious surface; and 
(28)  Locate all viable trees over eight inches in diameter on the plat. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(405), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-465. - Specification for construction plans for expansion/addition to existing commercial or industrial sites. 
Construction plans for expansions and/or additions to existing commercial or industrial sites, which do not expand or add more than 5,000 square feet of impervious surface and do not add additional or multiple stories must meet the minimum standards of design set forth in this article and must include the following: 
(1)  A letter requesting review and approval of the construction plans for the expansion or addition, giving the name; address and telephone number of the developer submitting the plan; 
(2)  Name and location of the development; 
(3)  Name, address, telephone number and seal of person preparing the plan for expansion or addition; 
(4)  Date, scale, north arrow and number of sheets; 
(5)  Locations and dimensions of all existing structures (principal and accessory); 
(6)  Location and dimensions of the proposed expansion or addition; 
(7)  Minimum yards and setbacks specified in the zoning ordinance; 
(8)  Exits, entrances, internal circulation patterns showing traffic lanes, fire lanes and acceleration/deceleration lanes, only if being modified or changes as a result of the expansion or addition; 
(9)  Parking layout, including handicapped parking and landscaping, only if being modified or changes as a result of the expansion or addition; 
(10)  Off-street loading, only if being modified or changes as a result of the expansion or addition; 
(11)  Location of refuse collection and any outside storage and/or service areas, and how such refuse and storage areas will be screened, only if being modified or changed as a result of the expansion or addition; 
(12)  Water and sanitary sewer plans (if applicable) which comply with all city development standards, only if being modified or changes as a result of the expansion or addition; 
(13)  A specification chart on the plans with all pipe gauges and other pertinent specifications; and 
(14)  Site grading plan with soil erosion and sedimentation control plan. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(406), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-466. - Other required plans. 
The following may be submitted with a site plan or may be submitted separately; however, no clearing, grubbing or grading shall be undertaken until a land disturbance permit has been approved and visibly posted at the primary point of access to the property: 
(1)  Building plans (four sets); 
(2)  Landscape, buffer and screening plan (nine sets); 
(3)  Grading and soil erosion plan (nine sets); 
(4)  Hydrological study (two sets); 
(5)  Water and sewer plan (nine sets); 
(6)  Sign plan (three sets); and 
(7)  Facade elevations (three sets for city use or eight sets if review by the mayor and council is requested. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(407), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-467. - Development standards for utility installations. 
(a)  Utility easements. When it is found to be necessary and desirable to locate public utility lines in other than street rights-of-way, easements must be shown on the plat for utility purposes. Such easements must not be less than 20 feet wide and, where possible, must be centered on rear or side lot lines. All utility easements shall comply with the minimum standards as specified by the utility provider. 
(b)  Water supply systems. 
(1)  Public water system. If available, the proposed development must be connected to a public water supply and water mains, fire hydrants and stub connections must be shown on the construction plans. 
(2)  Private water supply system. If public water supply is not available, the developer may install a private water system developed according to plans and specifications shown on the approved construction plans and approved by the city. 
(c)  Sanitary sewer disposal systems. 
(1)  Public sewage system. If available, the proposed development must be connected to a public sewage system and sewage mains and stub connections must be shown on the construction plans. If a lift station is required the developer must pay the cost of the station. 
(2)  Individual sewage system. When a public sewage system is not available the developer must carefully consider the capability and suitability of the general area of the property to support an individual sewage system (septic tanks). Such proposed sewage system must be approved by the Lamar County Health Department. The city must consider the recommendation of the Lamar County Health Department regarding any proposed private sewage systems in approval of the construction plans. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(408), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-468. - Development standards for drainage facilities. 
(a)  Watercourse and drainage easements. Where a proposed development is traversed by a watercourse, drainage way or stream, appropriate provisions must be made to accommodate stormwater and drainage through and from the proposed development. Such an easement must conform substantially with the lines of the watercourse and be wide enough and of adequate construction to be satisfactory for the purpose. 
(b)  Detention facility maintenance. 
(1)  The stormwater detention storage capacity or function of any detention basin, pond or other impoundment, whether natural of manmade, shall not be removed or diminished without the city's express approval. 
(2)  It shall be the responsibility of the property owner to maintain the operational characteristics of any stormwater detention facility construction in the development pursuant to the requirements of this article and/or any other regulation enacted by the city for such purpose, and to maintain the detention facility free of obstruction, silt or debris. The detention facility perimeter must be fenced with six-foot-high fence. 
(3)  A certified record survey of each detention facility shall be prepared by a land surveyor currently registered in the State of Georgia. A certified record drawing of the facility shall be prepared based upon the survey. Based on the actual parameters established on the record drawing, an addendum to the stormwater management report shall be prepared which demonstrates that the facility, as constructed, complies with the requirements of this article and/or any other regulation enacted by the city for such purpose. The amendment stormwater management report shall be certified by a professional engineer currently registered in the State of Georgia, in accordance with the provisions of Georgia law. Such certification shall substantially comply with the following form: 
Detention Pond Certification Form 
Date: ________ 
To: CITY OF MILNER BUILDING INSPECTION DEPARTMENT 
Project Name: ___________ 
Designed Storage Volume: ___________ 
As Built Storage Volume: ___________ 
(Provide 8½ × 11 drawing of designed outlet structure and as build outlet structure.) 
By placing my professional stamp and signature hereon, I certify that this detention pond is constructed according to the approved design on file with the City of Milner and on record at the City of Milner Building Inspection Department. I further certify that all the drainage area designed to drain to this pond in fact does drain to said pond and the outflow from the pond is equal to or less than the maximum allowable outflow for the 10 and 100 year storm events. Calculations to determine the as-built storage volume shall be maintained by me and provided to City of Milner in the event they are needed by City of Milner to verify this volume capacity. 

 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(409), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-469. - Development standards for driveway entrances. 
Driveway construction for commercial/industrial developments adjoining a city or county road shall consist of six inches of DOT 3000 PSI concrete or the specifications illustrated in exhibit "A", attached hereto. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(410), 11-16-2009) 
Editor's note— Exhibit A, as referenced above, is on file with the offices of the city. 
Sec. 118-470. - Certifications. 
The following certificates shall be inscribed on the construction plans: 
(1)  Engineer. 
I hereby certify that the engineering requirements for these construction documents as prescribed by the Commercial/Industrial Development Ordinance of the City of Milner, Georgia, have been fulfilled. 
___________(Name)  Registered Professional Engineer No._______ 
Date: ________ 
(2)  Administrative officer. 
I hereby certify that this construction plan was approved by the City of Milner, Georgia on ________ (date). 
___________(Name)  Administrative officer 
(3)  Property owner. 
I hereby understand that approval of this construction plan is valid for a period of two years. Any application for a building permit submitted after the time has lapsed shall not be accepted. Construction plans should be resubmitted and should conform to the current adopted standards (as of the date of resubmittal) of the City of Milner, Georgia. Review fees will apply. 
___________(Name)  Property owner 
Date: ________ 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(411), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-471. - Site plan revisions. 
Any deviation or revisions from approved site and/or construction plans must be shown on revised site and/or construction plans approved by the administrative officer. Changes shall be authorized in writing on the revised site and/or construction plans by the administrative officer. A copy of the revised plan(s) shall be retained by the administrative officer for inclusion in the development file. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(412), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-472. - Certificate of occupancy. 
In no case shall a certificate of occupancy be issued by the administrative officer unless an as-built condition is reflected on approved site and/or development plan. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(413), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-473—118-479. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - ARCHITECTURAL AND DESIGN STANDARDS 

Sec. 118-480. - Objectives. 
In order to maintain high quality, long-lasting and sustainable commercial/industrial development within the city, the city adopts design criteria for all newly constructed nonresidential buildings, intended to encourage an "old town" look and feel of historic Georgia villages. The guidelines in this division will foster architectural diversity and interest, yet achieve and maintain a consistent, durable and pleasing aesthetic/visual quality. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(501), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-481. - Building materials. 
The use of a common palate of building materials should be maintained for all building facades to create a consistent and traditional architectural identity. Traditional architecture includes the use of brick, pitched roofs, low-profile signage and subdued colors. For large commercial/industrial retail buildings, variations in facade, roofline and depth shall be provided to lend the appearance of multi-tenant occupancy. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(502), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-482. - Facade elevation criteria. 
(a)  Facade elevations shall be submitted as a part of the request for approval of construction plans for the development. Facade elevations shall clearly indicate the proposed building materials and colors for each facade described therein. The plans shall clearly show the location and calculate the amount/percentage of all building materials included within each facade. 
(b)  Groups of buildings located within the development may be reviewed and approved as a single development, rather than as individual buildings. Grouping of buildings is encouraged to minimize the number of reviews required and to allow for originality and design flexibility. 
(c)  Allowed building materials. The following facade materials shall be allowed: 
(1)  Facades visible to a public street: Brick, stone, split faced concrete masonry unit (CMU), cement plank (Hardy Plank) siding, glass, stucco as exterior finish properly installed with appropriate vapor barrier. 
(2)  Facades not visible to a public street: Painted concrete block, painted formed concrete or prefabricated metal panel. 
(3)  Any building material allowed may be used in any percentage throughout the building. 
(d)  Accent/trim exterior building materials: Small amounts of building materials such as wood, tile, stucco, etc., may be used to enhance the elevation of the building or for decorative elements, not exceeding ten percent of the total wall area per facade. Neon tubing or similarly shaped light fixture is not an acceptable accent/trim building material. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(503), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-483. - Roof requirements. 
(a)  Pitched roofs. All one-story buildings less than 10,000 gross square feet must have a pitched roof between 4:12 and 12:12. If a pitched roof is not possible, a combination of flat roof and pitched roof is required, providing a pitched roof on the front and side of the building to screen any flat portion of the roof from view. The development may include arcades, drive-under canopies, porches and other features with the pitched roof. Materials for pitched roofs shall be limited to architectural dimensional grade asphalt shingles, natural slate, natural terra cotta, natural wood shake, copper or factory-finished sheet metal. 
(b)  Mansard roofs. Mansard roofs shall have a maximum pitch of 12:12 with a minimum six feet vertical surface length. 
(c)  Flat roofs. Flat roofs may be of any material that meets the City's Code. Exposed metal flashing shall be copper or factory-finished sheet metal. If factory-finished metal flashing is used, such as standing seam, the color must be an earth tone to blend with other materials or of a color to simulate weathered copper or bronze. All buildings with flat roofs should include parapet articulation on the front facade thereof. Roof articulations/offsets shall be at a minimum of one per each 125 linear feet of length by a change in the top line of the parapet. Additional articulation may occur at any lesser distance. If the front facade is less than 125 linear feet, a minimum of one roof articulation must be present. 
(d)  Other. Drive-under canopies for gasoline pumps shall have a pitched roof consistent with the pitched roof material requirements in paragraph (a), above. The materials, ratio and color of the gas canopies' pitched roof shall be consistent with any associated primary structure. Where a full pitch is not possible, a hip roof may be provided. In such situations, a minimum 3:12 roof pitch shall be maintained. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(504), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-484. - Arcade/structural canopy—Retail use. 
A covered arcade/structural canopy shall be provided along the front facade of each multi-tenant commercial shopping or strip center. Arcades are covered walkways connected to or separate from the principal building. Arcades/canopies must be designed in a manner which provides architectural depth to the building and includes covered areas for relief from the weather. The arcade/canopy must be a minimum of five feet in width. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(505), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-485. - Vents/HVAC and other equipment. 
All mechanical equipment, including meters, rooftop equipment, fan units and vents shall be placed on a non-street side or screened from public view. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(506), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-486. - Temporary buildings. 
Temporary buildings or mobile buildings, including, but not limited to, trailers, campers, recreational vehicles and tents, shall not be allowed within public view with the exception of authorized dealerships of such buildings and temporary trailers associated with approved developments. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(507), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-487. - Buildings in excess of 30,000 square feet. 
For single-story commercial or industrial buildings exceeding 30,000 square feet of heated space, the following design criteria apply in addition to those listed above: 
(1)  Facades greater than 100 feet in length, measured horizontally, shall incorporate wall plan projections or recesses having a depth of at least three percent of the length of the facade and extending at least 20 percent of the length of the facade. No uninterrupted length of any facade shall exceed 100 horizontal feet. 
(2)  Ground-floor facades that face public streets shall have arcades, display windows, entry areas, awnings, or other such features along no less than 60 percent of their horizontal length. 
(3)  Building facades must include a repeating pattern that shall include no less than three of the following elements: color change, texture change, material change, or expression of architectural or structural bay through a change in plan no less than 24 inches in width, such as an offset, reveal or projecting rib. All elements shall repeat at intervals of no more than 30 feet, either horizontally or vertically. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(508), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-488. - Energy conservation. 
Construction of all structures shall comply with the requirements of the 2006 International Energy Conservation Code. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(509), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-489—118-499. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - DOWNTOWN DEVELOPMENT AUTHORITY OVERLAY DISTRICT REQUIREMENTS 

Sec. 118-500. - Objectives. 
In order to maintain high quality, long-lasting and sustainable commercial development within the downtown development authority ("DDA") overlay district, the city adopts additional architectural design criteria for all newly constructed nonresidential buildings, as well as any substantial renovations of existing structures located therein. The additional architectural design criteria are intended to encourage and further enhance the "old town" look and feel of city's commercial village. To the extent the provisions of this division may conflict with other requirements of this article, the provisions of this division shall control development within the DDA overlay district. Examples of structures which, if constructed, satisfy the interest of this division are shown in photographs, attached hereto as exhibit "B" and which are incorporated herein. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(601), 11-16-2009) 
Editor's note— Exhibit B, as referenced above, is on file with the offices of the city. 
Sec. 118-501. - Substantial renovation. 
The purpose of this division, "substantial renovation" shall mean any modification or repair to an existing structure, the cost for which equals at least 50 percent of the fair market value of the existing structure. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(602), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-502. - Maximum square footage. 
The maximum heated square footage of any structure shall not exceed 5,000 square feet. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(603), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-503. - Building height. 
No building shall exceed 30 feet in height. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(604), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-504. - Location of buildings and sidewalks. 
Any new building or structure which fronts on Main Street shall be constructed along Main Street not to exceed more than 60 feet from the centerline, so long as consistent with the location of existing buildings. The developer shall also construct a sidewalk at the front of each building from the right-of-way to front facade thereof of at least ten feet in width, so long as consistent with that of adjoining structure. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(605), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-505. - Roofs. 
Roofs on each building shall slope from front to back, with the front roofline being hidden by a false architectural facade on the building. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(606), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-506. - Building materials/color. 
All building architectural plans, along with material and paint samples shall be submitted to the downtown development authority for approval consistent with the provisions of this division. The downtown development authority shall notify the administrative officer of compliance before any building permit shall be issued. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(607), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-507. - Building materials permitted on side walls. 
Any side wall visible to the public shall be constructed of brick, stone, split-faced concrete masonry unit (CMU), cement plank (hardy plank) siding, glass, stucco as exterior finish, properly installed with appropriate vapor barrier. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(608), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-508. - Doors/windows. 
All doors and windows shall be composed of wood or color anodized aluminum. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(609), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-509. - Utilities. 
All utilities shall be located underground. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(610), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-510. - Utility fixtures/on-site loading and storage. 
All loading docks and utility fixtures must be located at the rear of any structure. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(611), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-511. - Energy conservation. 
Construction of all structures shall comply with the requirements of the 2006 International Energy Conservation Code. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(612), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-512—118-519. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - ENFORCEMENT/VARIANCE 

Sec. 118-520. - Alternate review. 
Requests to vary the requirements of this article or the request for approval of alternative design proposals must be approved by the mayor and council at a public meeting. The city may require additional information, including, but not limited to, presentation of material samples and facade mock-ups in order to determine whether the alternative proposal satisfies the intent of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(701), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-521. - Administrative modifications. 
In the event the intent of this division can be achieved with only minor deviations from the express provisions contained herein which do not substantially impact the goals or intent of this article, the administrative officer may modify the specific provisions. The mayor and council may, as part of any approval of any plan submitted pursuant to this division, impose conditions, modifications or additional requirements as necessary to mitigate any part of the development plan. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(702), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-522. - Appeals and variances. 
Appeals and variances from the requirements of this article shall be brought pursuant to the procedures set forth in article II of the city's zoning ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(703), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-523. - Penalties. 
Any person who violates any provision of this article or any amendment hereto, or who fails to perform any act required hereunder or commits any prohibited act shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punishable by a fine of not more than $1,000.00 for each offense. Each and every day for which any violation is committed or permitted to continue, shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such hereunder. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(704), 11-16-2009) 
Secs. 118-524—118-529. - Reserved.

Sec. 118-530. - Downtown development authority overlay zone map. 
The official downtown development authority overlay zone map is hereby incorporated into and made a part of this article. Any reference to the downtown development authority overlay zone map refers thereto. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(801), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-531. - Identification of the official map. 
The official downtown development authority overlay zone map is signed by the mayor and bears the seal of the city or that of a notary public under the following words: "This certifies that this is the official downtown development authority overlay zone map, referred to in division 8 of the "Commercial/Industrial Development Ordinance of the City of Milner, Georgia," together with the date of adoption of the ordinance from which this article derives. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(802), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-532. - Amendment to the official map. 
The modification or amendment to the official downtown development authority overlay zone map is an amendment to the article. The procedure by which amendments are proposed and approved is set forth in article II of the city's zoning ordinance. Any amendment must be entered onto the official map as soon as the amendment has been approved by the mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(803), 11-16-2009) 
Sec. 118-533. - Display of the official map. 
The official downtown development authority overlay zone map shall be on display in the office of the administrative officer, and the official map is the final authority regarding the status of the downtown development authority overlay zone's boundaries. 
(Ord. No. 2009-3, § 1(804), 11-16-2009)
